## Page 1

## CHAPTER X11-1

RECEIVABLES INQUIRY

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to review customer information including:

— source information entered in Receivables Maintenance

- statistics on the last invoice, the last payment, the last interest charged, and the
last letter sent to each customer

— asummary history, from the first entry, of all invoices, payments and
discounts for each customer

~— all current and history transactions for each customer

— transaction detail for each invoice and payment

### Entrance Screen

O From the Receivables Menu (XI-1), select option 1, Receivables Inquiry, and
press [Enter]. If the Receivables Security Gate appears, enter your division
code and security code and press [Enter]. The Receivables Inquiry, Screen #1
screen appears.

Screen A: Receivables Inquiry, Screen # 1

How to Find a Receivable

By Address Number

C1 Type the customer’s address number in the “Address #” field and press
[Enter]. The information on the receivable will appear.

By Customer Name

O Leave the “Address #” field blank, and type the first letters of the customer’s
name in the “Alpha” field. Press [Enter]. The Receivables Inquiry, Customer
Index appears.

O To change receivables, type a new address number or a new customer name.

O] The list of receivables is in alphabetical order beginning with the letters you
have typed in the “Alpha” field.

Ci To scroll through the pages of the screen, press the roll keys.

OF To select one of the receivables on the list, type any character in the column to
the left of the customer’s name.

0 Information on the receivable will be display automatically in Receivables
Inquiry, Screen #1.

automatically generated by the system. The user can not modify them.

Screen C: Receivables Inquiry, Screen # 1 - Customer Selected

Descriptions of fields of the screen:

### Field Description

Address # The address number of the customer.

Alpha To use the Customer Index, enter the first letters of
the customer’s name and press [Enter]. Leave the
“Address #” field blank.

Print To enable the Print Transactions Register option,

type ¥ in this field and press [Enter]. The Y does
not remain in the field. When you press [Cmd1]-
End, to exit the procedure, the Transaction Registers
screen will appear.

Kame The name of the customer.

Name (Ext) The extension of the name of the customer. Can be
used to include the owner or manager’s name when
the “Name” of the customer is a company.

Address The postal address of the customer.

Address (Ext) The extension of the address.

address.

The method to used calculate the GST. Canadian
customers only.

Sort Codes are used to sort customers for
applications such as Marketing (Menu X4) and Print
Letters (X11-13). Sort codes are defined in Address
Maintenance (X4-2).

1 character. Customer Rank. Advanced Rentals
only. Dealer assigned. Optional.

is: http://www.epa.gov/enviro/html/codes/state.html

Information, entered by you, about this customer.
The total balance that is due from this customer.
The date that determines the age of receivables for
this customer. Aging is calculated automatically
when you inquire on a customer. Aging is calculated
automatically for all customers each time that you
Tun the end of day procedures. You can calculate
aging for all customers from the option, Calculate
Receivables Age (X11-15).

The amount of the balance currently due.

The amount past due by 31 to 60 days.

The amount past due by 61 to 90 days.

The amount past due by 91 to 120 days.

The amount past due by 121 days or more.

The amount of interest included in the total balance.
The highest balance ever owed by the receivable.
The number of the general ledger account for this
teceivables customer.

The maximum credit to be extended to the
customer. The amount prints in dollars without
decimals. This amount is set up under Receivables
Maintenance (X11-2) and appears in Point Of Sale
(X5-1) and Receivables Inquiry (X11-1). To set up
your system to stop Point of Sale billing for
customers who have exceeded their credit limit, see
the instructions in the “Credit Limit” field
description in Chapter X11-2, Receivables
Maintenance.

The central address number of the customer when
the customer has multiple stores. To print one
Statement for all stores using the same corporate
address see the “Print?” field below.

The code for the statement type. Determines how
transactions display on the statement.

O = Open item.

B = Balance forward.

The print statement code.

Y = Statements for this customer will print when
you run Print Statements (X11-10 or X11-11)

N = Statements will not be printed for this
customer.


&

X11-1 » RECEIVABLES INQUIRY

Credit Codes

Tax/SIC Code
C = Print statements under the corporate address (if
applicable).

Credit codes identify the credit status for this
customer and are used at Point of Sale. Credit codes
are set up in the option Credit Code Maintenance
(X68-1). You can enter up to two credit codes per
customer in Receivables Maintenance (X11-2).
Messages set up for these codes blink on the “Point
Of Sale-Sold To” screen. The following credit codes
are preset in your system, though you can set up
others.

Code Message

Never Charge

Cash Only

No Interest Charged

Credit Not Established

30 Days Past Due

60 Days Past Due

90 Days Past Due

120 Days Past Due

Credit Limit

The credit code “Z” means “Do not
invoice this customer” and the billing is stopped
automatically at Point Of Sale.

Tax Code = 1 character. The default tax code for
the customer. Set up in Tax configuration
Maintenance (X52-7), and assigned to customers in
Receivables Maintenance (X11-2) and in Work
With Customers (X9-4).

SIC Code = 4 digits. Standard Industrial
Classification code. Each 4-digit code represents a
unique business activity.

Screen D: Screen #2

Descriptions of fields of the screen:

### Field Description

Address # The address number of the customer.

Alpha To use the Customer Index, enter the first letters of
the customer’s name and press [Enter]. Leave the
“Address #” field blank.

Print To enable the print transactions register option, type

¥ in this field and press [Enter]. The Y does not
remain in the field. When you press [Cmd1i]-End, to
exit the procedure, the Transaction Registers screen
will appear.


X11-1 « RECEIVABLES INQUIRY

Interest:
Charge Interest

Annual Percentage Rate

Number of Days
to Charge Interest

Basic Service Charge

Round Up To
Basic Service Charge

Number of Days That
Make Collection Critical
Group Code

Service Code
The default is Y (Yes). N (No) means that you do
not want to charge interest to this customer.

The annual interest percentage rate entered in
Security Maintenance (X6-6) for the division. Can
be changed in Receivables Maintenance for this
customer. Example: “01800” = 18%.

The number of days from the invoice date when
interest will begin to be charged. The system will
determine the number of days for calculating
interest in the following order:

1. Transaction, as specified in Apply Credits (X11-
4)

2. Customer, as specified in Receivables
Maintenance (X11-2)

3. Division, as specified in Security Maintenance
(X6-6) for all the receivables

4. If all these fields are blank, the default will be 30
days.

The basic (minimum) service charge, entered in
Security Maintenance (X6-6) for the division. Can
be changed in Receivables Maintenance for this
customer, Example: “100” = $1.00.

Y = The amount of interest charged is rounded

up to the basic (minimum) service charge if it is less
than the minimum.

N=No interest is charged if the amount of interest
is less than the minimum.

The number of days past due where collection
becomes critical for this customer.

The group code (if any) assigned to this receivable
customer. Group codes are created under Group
Code Maintenance (X11-3).

Service codes allow you to split transactions
between the customer, yourself, and warrantors.
One of the following defines this customer:
Customer

Internal address

Warranty address

Service codes are used in Point Of Sale and Service
Management. For a full discussion of service codes,
see the “Warranty & Internal Charges” section in
Chapter X5-1, Point of Sale Invoicing.

Screen F: Summary History

On this screen, you can see a summary history from the first entry, of all invoices,
payments and discounts for each customer:

- Number and total amount of transactions per month

— Number and total amount of payments per month

~ Average age of payments for life of customer

- Year-to-Date GST and PST (Canada only)

The amounts are listed by general ledger posting month. You can use the [PgUp]
and [Page Down] keys to see other years.

Descriptions of fields of the screen:

### Field Description

Alpha To use the Customer Index, enter the first letters of
the customer’s name and press [Enter]. Leave the
“Address #” field blank.

Y in this field and press [Enter]. The Y does not

concerning the displayed customer. Notes can be printed independently, and the
first 3 lines of notes can be printed on the Aged Receivables Collection Report

(X11.14-3).

Maintenance (X11-2) and to add new notes to a customer account, from
Receivables Inquiry, Screen #1, Screen #2, or the Statistics screen, press

Screen H: Edit Address Notes.

This screen displays existing notes. Once a note is created, it can only be modified
in Receivables Maintenance (X11-2).

O To delete a note, type 4 (Delete) in the “Opt” field and press [Enter].


16 X11-1 » RECEIVABLES INQUIRY RELEASE 2.2

 

### Warning!

Once you select a note to be deleted and press [Enter], the note is, deleted. There is
not a confirmation screen.

 

0 To add a new note, press [F6]=Add. A “Note” field appears. Type the note in
the “Note” field and press [Enter]. The note is recorded and an empty note
field appears. To retum to the Display Address Notes screen, press [F3]=Exit.
The Display Address Notes screen appears and displays the note you just
created.

O To retum to the Receivables Inquiry screen, press [F3]=Exit.

Sereen |: Transactions, Page 1

### X11-1 ¢ Receivables Inquiry 7

O This screen displays receivable transactions by stock number. To switch the
view between stock number and due date, press [Cmd8] - Due Date.

O This screen displays receivable transactions by invoice date. To switch the
view between invoice date and invoice number, press [Cmd9] - Invoice

Number.

O The information for each transaction is displayed over three pages. To access
Page 2, press Cmd12-Page 2.

Descriptions of fields of the screen (Transactions, Page 1):

Description

The address number of the customer.

To use the Customer Index, enter the first letters of
the customer’s name and press [Enter]. Leave the
“Address #” field blank.

To enable the print transactions register option, type
¥ in this field and press [Enter]. The Y does not
remain in the field. When you press {Cmd1]-End, to
exit the procedure, the Transaction Registers screen
will appear.

Enter the date (if the screen displays transactions by
date) or the invoice number (if the screen displays
transactions by invoice number) to begin the list of
transactions with a specific transaction.

The date of the invoice.

The invoice number.

The description of the invoice.

The general ledger month for posting the invoice.
The stock number for the invoice.

customer.

in dollars without decimais. This amount is set up

this customer. A default for all customers is set up

customers in Receivables Maintenance (X11-2).
“01800” = 18%.

## CHAPTER X11-2

RECEIVABLES MAINTENANCE

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to:

— open receivable accounts for new customers

— modify information on established receivable accounts, including credit card
information

— delete customer accounts
Customer address numbers cannot be removed from the system as long as
there are any documents for them in the document index in Point of Sale. Ta
purge P.O.S. documents, run end of Month Procedures (X5-4).

In addition, you can maintain an unlimited number of note lines for each

customer.

### Contents

number can have a maximum of six (6) letters and characters. All combinations
are allowed.

### X11-2 ¢ Receivables Maintenance 5

To add a note to the customer account, press [Cmd6] - Note.
To print the note for this customer account, press [Cmd7] - Print Note.

To display a list of a customer’s credit cards, press [Cmd8] - Credit Cards. An
accounting security gate prevents unauthorized users from having access to
confidential information. This security gate is always displayed after you press
Cmd8.

FIELDS AND DESCRIPTIONS (IN ALPHABETICAL ORDER)

Descriptions of fields in the Receivables Maintenance data entry screens:

Field
120 days past

Annual Percentage Rate

Description

System generated. The amount past due by 121 days
or More.

System generated. The amount past due by 31 to 60
days.

System generated. The amount past due by 61 to 90
days.

System generated. The amount past due by 91 to
120 days.

The general ledger account number you set up for
this receivables customer.

28 characters. The name of the person responsible
for accounts payable at this customer.

6 characters. The customer identifying number.
Defaults from the previous screen.

20 characters. The postal address (street address or
PO box) of the customer.

20 characters. Additional address information, if
needed.

Date (mmddyy) on which aging was last calculated
for this customer. Updated for all customers at the
Accounting End of Day, or from the option
Calculate Receivables Age (X11-15). To update for
this customer only, press [Cmd10] - Calc Age.

17 characters. The name of the agent at the
insurance agency.

5 digits. The annual interest percentage rate entered
in Security Maintenance (X6-6) for the division.
Can be changed in Receivables Maintenance for this
customer. The Annual Percentage Rate assumes 4
decimal places: you'll enter 18% as 1800 and press
[Field Exit]. When the annual rate is 18%, the
monthly rate is 1.5% (18/12). You can assign
different interest rates to each customer, and it is
also possible to assign a different number of days
before interest charges begin (see Number of Days
To Charge Interest).


Basic Service Charge

Charge Interest

City, State
Corp Address

Credit Codes

X11-2 ¢ RECEIVABLES MAINTENANCE 9

5 digits. The basic (minimum) service charge,
entered in Security Maintenance (X6-6) for the
division. Can be changed here for this customer.
Example: “00100” = $1.00.

The default is Y (Yes). N (No) means that you do
not want to charge interest to this customer.

20 characters. City and state of customer’s address.
6 characters. The central address number of the
customer when the customer has multiple stores. To
use the corporate address feature, it must be
activated by tuming on the Corporate Address OPT
(X6374-4). Any number of receivables can be
attached to the same corporate address. When
statements are printed the statements associated
with the corporate address are printed together. See
the “Sample Corporate Statement” at the end of this
chapter. To print one statement for all stores using
the same corporate address see the “Print?” field
below.

Credit codes identify the credit status for this
customer and are used at Point of Sale. Credit codes
are set up in the option Credit Code Maintenance
(%68-1). You can enter up to two credit codes per
customer here in Receivables Maintenance.
Messages set up for these codes blink on the “Point
Of Sale-Sold To” screen. The following credit codes
are preset in your system, though you can set up
others.

Code Message

Never Charge

Cash Only

No Interest Charged

Credit Not Established

30 Days Past Due

60 Days Past Due

90 Days Past Due

120 Days Past Due

Credit Limit

The credit code “Z” means “Do not invoice
this customer” and the billing is stopped
automatically at Point Of Sale.

To set up your system to stop Point of Sale billing
for customers that have exceeded their credit limit,
you must first create a “Z” credit code under the
option Credit Code Maintenance (X68-1). Then go
to the OPTDIS Master Menu (X6-3). Find the
“Lockout” feature in OPT Point of Sale Menu Ten
(X636A) and choose “Lockout is installed
(manual)” or “Lockout is installed (automatic).”
Automatic lockout means that for all accounts, (
Point of Sale billing wili be stopped when the
account exceeds the credit limit set for that
customer. When the account returns to below the set
credit limit, the system automatically removes the
“Z” credit code, reinstating Point of Sale billing.
Manual lockout means that for all! accounts, Point of
Sale billing will only be stopped when you set the
credit code for that account to “Z” here in
Receivables Maintenance. To release Point of Sale
billing for that account, you must manually remove
the “Z” credit code from the account in Receivables
Maintenance.

only. Dealer assigned. Optional.

rental insurance policy. Y = Yes, N = No.
1 character. Discount Code. Discount codes are set
up in Discount Maintenance (X52-6) and assigned
to customers here in Receivables Maintenance and
in Work With Customers (X9-4). (

1 character. Service codes allow you to split

State and County Federal Information Processing

State FIPS code = 2 digits. County FIPS = 3 digits.
To look up a FIPS code on the Internet, the address
is: http://www.epa.gov/enviro/html/codes/state.html
1 character (O/B). Required. The code for the
statement type. Determines how transactions display
on the statement. Can be changed anytime.

O = Open item.

B = Balance forward.

NOTE: Transactions are maintained by the system as Open Item. The statement

type can be changed at any time to Balance Forward or vice versa.

The tax ID number of the customer.

customer. Set up in Tax configuration Maintenance
(X52-7), and assigned to customers in Receivables
Maintenance (X11-2) and in Work With Customers
(X9-4).

SIC Code = 4 digits. Standard Industrial
Classification code. Each 4-digit code represents a
unique business activity.

The telephone number of the accounts payable
clerk.

The home telephone number of the customer.

The zip code.


ACCOUNTING X11-2 » RECEIVABLES MAINTENANCE 15
EACLE MAINFENANCE

DELETE A RECEIVABLE ACCOUNT

### Warning!

The system will only allow you to delete a customer (and the “To delete enter

“Y’” field will only be present) if the customer account has a zero total balance,
and the account has no history (either there were no transactions on this account,
or history for this account was purged in End of Year Receivables File
Maintenance (X1.12-5)).

 

O To delete a receivable account, from the first page of the Receivables
Maintenance screen, type ¥ in the “To delete enter ‘Y’” field and press
[Enter]. The receivable account will no longer appear on Teports or in the
Customer Index. The account is not permanently deleted until you run “Purge
Deleted Receivables” in the Receivables File Maintenance option under the
End of Year Menu (X1.12-5), which purges by merge G/L month.

### Reinstate A Deleted Account

O To reinstate a customer account that has been deleted in Receivables
Maintenance, but has not been purged in End-of- Year Receivables File
Maintenance (X1.12-5), enter the address number in the Receivables
Maintenance entrance screen and press [Enter]. To reinstate the account, type
¥ in the “To reinstate enter ‘Y’” field.

Note

O To add or modify notes on the receivable account, from any Receivables
Maintenance screen, press [Cmd6] - Note. The Display Address Notes
window appears.

In this screen you can modify and delete existing notes. Notes can be created and

deleted in Receivables Maintenance and in Receivables Inquiry (X11-1), but notes

can only be edited in Receivables Maintenance.

O To modify an existing note, type the new information on the line containing
the note.

Ci To delete a note, type 4 (Delete) in the “Opt” field and press [Enter}.

WARNING! Once you select a note to be deleted and press [Enter], the note is

deleted. There is not a confirmation screen.

 

O01 To add a new note, press [F6}=Add. A “Note” field appears. Type the note in
the “Note” field and press [Enter]. The note is recorded and an empty note
field appears. To return to the Display Address Notes screen, press [F3]=Exit.
The Display Address Notes screen appears and displays the note you just
created.

O To retum to the Receivables Inquiry screen, press [F3]=Exit.

O To print the notes for a customer, press [Cmd7] - Print Note. The notes are
printed and a “Note Printed” message displays at the bottom of the screen.

CREDIT CARD INFORMATION

Setting Up a Receivables Address for a Credit Card
0 From the Receivables Menu, select option 2, Receivables Maintenance.

O Create a new receivable address that will be easily identified, such as
CASCRE for Case Credit Card, FARMPL for Farm Plan, or MASTER and
VISA.

The following fields are important:
Account # — Use the new general ledger account number created.

Statement


18 X11-2 * RECEIVABLES MAINTENANCE RELEASE 2.2
eee eee EASE BE

Type B=Balance Forward or O=Open Item.
If you will be reconciling payments to your dealership from the
credit card company, make the address open item. This will allow
you to track each document. Note that it also means the credits will
need to be merged against the appropriate debits.

Tf you are not concerned about reconciling payments with
individual document charges, make the address balance forward.

Print? N. No statement will be printed.

Tax Code Assign the same tax code you give most other customers. Taxes
will be calculated based on the individual customer’s tax code, not
on the charge card tax code.

After credit cards have been set up, you’re ready to attach credit card information
to your customers’ master records in Receivables Maintenance. Both Case Credit
and Farm Plan card numbers can be captured at Point of Sale and automatically
added to the customer’s list of card numbers. Other credit cards can be stored in
Receivables Maintenance but can not be captured at Point of Sale.

O Press the new command key at the bottom of the screen: Cmd8-Credit Cards.
An accounting security gate prevents unauthorized users from having access to
confidential information. This security gate will always be displayed after you
press Cmd8.

O Type the 2-character credit card code and the customer’s card number
(without dashes or blanks) and expiration date.
You can record as many cards for each customer as needed. A customer can have
more than one account number for the same type of card, such as 2 different Visa
account numbers. Expiration dates equal to or less than 39 are considered to be
2000-2039; dates equal to or greater than 40 are considered to be 1940-1999,
Expiration dates are not required for Farm Plan/Agline cards. The default date for
Case Credit cards is 1299 (December 1999). You'll receive a warning message if
the expiration date is earlier than the current date.

first page of the Receivables Maintenance screen, press [Cmd10] - Calculate
Age. When you press {Cmd10] -Calculate Age, to calculate the age for this
customer only, the following window will appear:

## CHAPTER X11-3

GROUP CODE MAINTENANCE

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to let you create codes for your receivable accounts so
that you can specify which accounts will be included in receivable reports and
statements. This option adds to your flexibility in managing your customer
information.

In this option you are creating group codes. Once group codes set up, they are
assigned to individual customers through option X11-2 - Receivables
Maintenance.

### Warning!

To have one special group, you must have a non-blank group code on all
customers.

 

### Contents

 
 
 
  
 

ENTRANCE SCREEN
CREATE GROUP CODE.
MODIFY GROUP CODE.
DELETE GROUP CODE..
PRINT GROUP CODE LIST


2 X11-3 e GROUP CODE MAINTENANCE RELEASE 2.1

### Entrance Screen

O1 From the Receivables Menu (X1-1), select option 3, Group Code Maintenance
and press [Enter]. If the Security Gate screen appears, enter your Division
Code and Security Code and press [Enter]. The Group Code Maintenance
screen appears.

NW EQUIPMENT SALES GROUP CODE MAINTENANCE X13301-02
Division A

mdl-End

 

 

Screen A: Group Code Maintenance

### Create Group Code

A group code can be from | to 5 characters long and can include letters or
numbers. For example, you may choose “A” for all customers billed on the first of
the month, and “B” for all customers billed on the 15°, or “IN” for your in-state
{or in-country} customers, and “OUT” for your out-of-state customers.

O Enter a group code and press [Enter]. In the Group Code Maintenance screen a
“Description” field appears.

Screen B: Group Code Maintenance - Description

A group code description is required for each group code. The description can be
up to 15 characters long and can include letters, numbers, and spaces.

O Enter a description for your group code and press [Enter].
OQ) To return to the “Group Code” field without update, Press [Cmd3] - Return.

O You can now enter additional group codes or, to return to the Receivables
Menu, press [Cmd1] - End.

### Modify Group Code

Group codes can be added or deleted only. Group code descriptions, however, can
be changed.

1 From the Group Code Maintenance screen enter the name of the group code to
be modified and press [Enter]. The group code description appears. If this is a
new group code the description line will be blank.

0) Type the changes to the description and press [Enter]. The group code is
updated.

## CHAPTER X11-4

APPLY CREDITS

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to merge payments (credits) with their
corresponding invoices (debits) and to change the number of days for calculating
interest for a particular invoice.

If you have entered receivables credits in Create Source Documents (X1-7) or
Point Of Sale Invoicing (X5-1), you will merge them with the corresponding
debits. If you enter all your payments from the Enter Payments (X1 1-5), you will
use this option to merge the debits and credits.

Note: The merge applies to all customers regardless of their “Statement Type”
(“O” = Open Item, or “B” = Balance Forward). This code determines how
transactions display on the statement. Credit and debit processing is exactly the
same for these two statement types.

Screen D: Change Days Of Interest - Customer Selected

This screen allows you to change the number of days used for calculating the
interest for a particular invoice. When you calculate the interest from the option
Calculate And Post Interest (X11-9), the system will determine the number of
days for calculating interest in the following order:
1. Transaction, as specified in the “Days Interest” field in Apply Credits
(X11-4)
2. Customer, as specified in “Number Of Days To Charge Interest” field in
Receivables Maintenance (X11-2)
3. Division, as specified in “Days Before Int” field in Security Maintenance
(X6-6) for all the receivables
4. Ifall these fields are blank, the default will be 30 days.

Transactions set to not charge interest for 999 days will be considered
“permanently current" and will never age regardless. The number of days until
interest begins can be set for the division in Security Maintenance, for the
customer in Receivables Maintenance, and for a particular transaction in Apply
Credits. See also Receivables OPTs. Otherwise, even though interest charges are
Postponed, transactions age normally. You might want to keep this in mind when
you compose messages that appear on statements. Aging cannot be changed.


X11-4 e APPLY CREDITS 7

O To change the number of days of interest, enter the transaction number in the
“Transaction” field and the number of days desired in the “Days Interest” field
and press [Enter]. The number that you have entered will appear in the “Dys”
field. :

O To remove the existing a number of days for a particular line, enter the
number of the transaction in the “Transaction” field and “O” in the “Days
Interest” field and press [Enter].

O If you never want to calculate the interest for a particular invoice, enter the
transaction number in the “Transaction” field and 999” in the “Days Interest”
field and press [Enter].

© Transactions are displayed by invoice number. To display transactions by
invoice date, press [Cmd9]- Invoice Number.

O Transactions are displayed with unit stock numbers. For corporate accounts, to
display transactions including the address number of the associated accounts,
press {Cmd10] - Addr#.

On a corporate address, such as Austin Construction Co., illustrated below, you
can press Cmd10-Address# to list the address numbers of the associated accounts,
so you’ll know who was responsible for the invoice.

Screen E: Merge

This screen allows you to merge transactions entered in Create Source Documents
(X1-7) or Point Of Sale Invoicing (X5-1). Each line that appears in this screen
represents a transaction that is a debit (invoice), or is a credit (payment) posted to
the account of the selected receivable. Credits appear as negative numbers.

Amounts to be merged display in the “Unpaid” column.

C1 To merge a debit and a credit, enter the line number of the first transaction in
the “Transaction #1” field and the line number of the second transaction in the
“Transaction #2” field and press [Enter].

To return to the “Change Days of Interest” screen, press [Cmd2}.
To display transactions by invoice number, press [Cmd9].
To scroll through the pages of the screen, press the roll keys.

Screen H: Automatic Merge

Parameter Selection

This screen allows you to select the automatic merge type that you prefer.
“Regular Merge” merges all eligible transactions for all customers by the
selected category. To be eligible for the regular merge, the first 8 characters of
the document number of the debit (invoice) have to be identical to first 8
characters of the credit description (payment). You can omit the #* at the end
of the document number that was generated in Point of Sale.

— “Merge In Balance Forward Mode” merges oldest debits with oldest credits
for all customers in the selected category.

You can select customers by general ledger account, group code, or by address

number for all automatic merge types.

. O Select options in the “Merge Type” and “Select by” fields and press [Enter] to
continue.

O To return to the “Selection” screen, press [Cmd3].

O To exit the procedure without applying credits, press [Cmd1] - End.

## CHAPTER X11-5

ENTER PAYMENTS

### Introduction

As the name indicates, Enter Payments is used to record accounts receivable
payments (checks), and other cash receipts and post them directly to the general
ledger You can also post write-offs directly to any number of general ledger
accounts as long as their edit codes are blank or "B." You can post discounts and
adjustments, and, in addition, the cash receipts feature allows you to post to other
accounts with edit codes, such as Accounts Payable (trade and flooring),
inventory, and scheduled accounts. Posting corrections are interactive (show up
on the screen as you make them). Regular Received on Account payments and
various cash receipts can be handled in the same batch.

Prior to entering payments for the first time, run Configure Payments (X11-6). It
will be easier to understand Enter Payments after you are introduced to Configure
Payments; therefore, these options will be discussed together in Configure
Payments (X11-6). The receipt types, accounts receivable payments, general
ledger levels, and the other default information are set up in Configure Payments.

### Warning!

Post payments before exiting or all payments entered will be lost.


2 X11-5 « ENTER PAYMENTS RELEASE 2.2

teceivable customer (by address number or name) or by selecting a Teceipt type.

will be displayed in this Enter Cash Receipts/A.R. Payments screen.

cash transactions. If you enter a receipt type, you can not also enter an address
number on this screen. If you select to enter a payment by receipt type rather than
by customer, you can not access customer information unless you know the
customer’s address number.

‘Screen H: Select Transactions

This screen displays current transactions for the selected customer. If a current
transaction is already used by another payment in the same batch, it will not
appear. You can see paid amounts and adjustments as well as the automatic
calculation of the amount applied (at the bottom of the screen). The general ledger
account for the adjustment will appear by default from Configure Payments (X11-
6). You can change the general ledger account in the Update G/L
Discounts/Adjustments Accounts screen ([Cmd6]).

There is a select transactions option for how transactions are applied to invoices.
To set the OPT, go to the OPTDIS Master Menu (X6-3) or see the Accounts
Receivable Guide to New Features.

O Enter or modify the amount paid for each transaction that you want to pay in
this batch. To automatically enter the correct amount of the transaction, press
the DUP key ([Shift]+[Insert]).

D Enter discount or adjustment amounts in the field “Disc/Adjustment.” The
DUP key is not available in the “Disc/Adjustment” fieid.


X11-5 ¢ ENTER PAYMENTS 15

 

o

If the payment is in balance, to accept the payment, press [Cmd3] - Return.
The Enter Cash Receipts/A.R. Payments screen will appear and you are ready
to enter the next payment. The transaction detail can not be greater that the
amount of the payment, and it can not be negative. If it is smaller than the
payment, the “Accept Payment” screen will appear. You can accept the
payment even if it is not completely applied. If the amount applied is negative
(more than the payment amount), an error message will display and you will
return to this screen.

To delete the payment, press [Cmd19] - Del Pymt.

To access the Update G/L Discounts/Adjustments Accounts screen, press
[Cmd6] - G/L Dis/Adj.

To change between the two modes of displaying transactions (by invoice
number or by date), press [Cmd9]. When you change modes, the system
automatically positions the list to the first transaction. Once you select a
display mode, the screen will continue to display in that mode, even if you
change customers.

To apply the payment automatically to invoices starting with the oldest
transaction, press [Cmd16] - Auto Apply.

To return to the A.R. Payment Information screen, press [Cmd5] - Payment
Info.

To position the list to the beginning of transactions, press the [Home] key.
To scroll through the pages of the screen, press the roll keys.

of the transaction. The amount has to be the same

Screen |: Apply Automatically

This screen allows you to modify the amount to apply automatically. The amount
of the payment entered in the A.R. Payment Information screen will appear by
default. If you modify the amount in this screen, the amount in the A.R. Payment
Information screen will not change.

Apply Automatically applies the payment to customer invoices automatically,
beginning with the oldest. Negative transactions are also applied. The payment is
applied to invoices unti] the payment is depleted. If an amount is already applied
to a transaction, this option does not modify it. Therefore, it is possible to apply
precise amounts to some transactions in the Select Transactions screen and then to
have Apply Automatically apply payments to the balance.

code is blank or "B."

completely applied. If the allocation is negative, you will receive an error message
and return to this screen.

## CHAPTER X11-6

CONFIGURE PAYMENTS

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to customize your payments. Under this
option you are able to set up receipt types, set up accounts receivable payments,
and set up levels in the general ledger. These defaults are in Enter Payments
(X11-5). It will be easier to understand Enter Payments after you have been
introduced to Configure Payments, therefore, in this chapter, these two options
will be discussed together.

DIS recommends that you post all cash and check receipts into a Cash on Hand
account during the day and transfer the total from Cash on Hand to Cash in Bank
when you make your daily deposit. This facilitates bank reconciliation because
there is just one transaction per day instead of the line-by-line detail.

### Contents

ACCOUNTS RECEIVABLE PAYMENTS ........-sssssssescssssessssesscsssessssnneesen 2

2 X11-6 « CONFIGURE PAYMENTS RELEASE 2.2

### Accounts Receivable Payments C

Accounts Receivable payments can be handled by customer address numbers and
matched to the corresponding invoices, which creates the cross reference Invoices
Paid By This Payment illustrated on page 7 and Payments Applied To This
Invoice illustrated on page 7. One check can be applied to one invoice per batch.
These payments are merged automatically. Unapplied credits can be posted, then
merged with an appropriate charge in a later batch.

 

Note
If a customer pays the unposted interest printed on a statement, post the unapplied
credit, then make a journal entry to post the interest. Use Apply Credits to merge
the payment with the interest.

 

The examples in this section will follow an Accounts Receivable payment from
beginning to end beginning with Configure Payments, where you’ ll find 3 options:

1-Receipt Types
2-A.R. Payments
3-Levels (optional). The system is shipped with the following levels which will be
sufficient: (
Level 1
Level 99

Levels refer to the amount of detail you want on the debit to the general ledger.
Level | generates only 1 debit, which is the total of all the credit lines whereas
Jevel 99 generates | line for each credit line. Level 99 is “hard-coded” and does
not have to be set up.

The second option, A.R. Payments, is where you provide the defaults that will be
used in Enter Payments if you start with a customer address number. A.R.
payments to a different bank or cash account can be handled easily by changing
the A.R. payment screen, which is illustrated below:


ACCOUNTING X11-6 ¢ CONFIGURE PAYMENTS 3

Level 1
generates 1
total debit
line for all
credit lines.

Level 99
generates 1
debit line for
each credit
line.

You can change the amounts to account for discounts or adjustments as illustrated
on line 2 or apply them to other invoices. After you have specified precise
amounts to go to individual invoices, press [EnterJor press Cmd16-Auto Apply to
apply the balance to transactions starting with the oldest. If an amount is already
applied to a transaction, this option does not modify it. Therefore, it is possible to
apply precise amounts to some transactions in the Select Transactions screen and
then to have Apply Automatically apply payments to the balance.

To reapply a payment or any portion of it, field exit through the amounts you want
to change, press [Enter], then press Cmd16-Auto Apply. If you forget to press
[Enter], nothing will change.

To change the discount/adjustment account, press Cmd6-G/L Dis/Adj.

When you are done, press Cmd3-Retum to go back to the entrance screen.

Note: OPT (X63-7) is available to automatically pay interest first on balance
forward.

not accumulate like Payables Invoice Entry.

### Cash Receipts (Optional)

For checks other than Received on Account, you may want to take advantage of
the optional Cash Receipts feature. For example, you may receive refunds or
rebates occasionally from various vendors, such as a utility company or a freight
carrier. The next screen illustrates the configuration screen for a receipt type for
rebates or refunds, debiting a bank account and crediting a variety of accounts.

X11-6 e CONFIGURE PAYMENTS

Notes:

## CHAPTER X11-7

ENTER WARRANTY PAYMENTS

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to enter warranty payments and to apply
them to the corresponding claims. You can also enter transactions to adjust the
differences between claim amounts and payment receipts or credits.

 

Note
You can process payments for a single warrantor per batch.

You may process payments for different claims from the warrantor who was

configured in Configure Warranty Payments (X1 1-8). You can also process claims
for other warrantors; however, there will be no default information for them.

### Contents

Screen C: Select Warranty Customer

The Select Warranty Customer screen allows you to select the customer for a
warranty payment. If you have entered an address number in the “Warranty
Customer Number’ field in Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8), that number
will appear here by default. You can change the address number. The address
number has to be valid as a receivable.

### Warning!

The warranty address number can not be changed after you have pressed [Enter]
in the Select Warranty Customer screen. Once a Warranty payment process has
begun, you have to cancel it, or post it before leaving this option.

field. To display the Customer Index, press [Enter].

CO To exit the procedure, press [Cmd1] - End. The current warranty payment will
be deleted. .

This screen allows you to enter the debit transaction for the warranty payment. If
the debit account, the description, or the address number is set up under Configure
Warranty Payments (X11-8), they will appear here by default.

The edit code for the general ledger account entered the “Debit Account” field
will determine which fields are required. See the field descriptions below or refer
to the “Create Source Documents Posting Guide” in Chapter X1-7.

O To continue, complete the fields of the screen and press [Enter].

O To cancel creating the payment and return to the Select Warranty Customer
screen, press [Cmd3] - Return. If a payment has already been created by
pressing [Enter], and you press [Cmd3] - Retum, an error message will appear
indicating that this command key is not available at this stage.

O1 To delete the warranty payment and exit the procedure, press [Cmd1] - End.
The current warranty payment will be deleted. The Receivables Menu (XI-1)

will appear.

Field
Debit Account

Document Number
Amount

Description

8 characters. Required. If a debit account is set up
under Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8), it will
appear here by default. The debit account has to be a
valid account in the general ledger. It can be in any
division, and can be any account type. Accounts
with edit codes “E”, “G” and “S” are not allowed.
10 characters. Required. The document number for
the debit.

9 digits. Required. The total amount of the debit.

12 characters. Required. If the description is set up
under Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8), it will
appear here by default.

6 characters. If the address number is set up under
Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8), it will
appear here by default. Otherwise, it is required for
a debit account with edit codes “A” (receivable),
“P” (payable) or “F” (flooring). If no address
number is required by the general ledger account,
you can enter it for reference.

6 digits. MMDDYY (month, day, year) format. The
due date is required for a debit account with edit
codes “P” or “F”. If the due date is not required by
the general ledger account, you can enter it for
reference.

and “Amount” must be the same sign (both positive
or both negative).

account, you can enter it as reference,

oo

Enter the document number to apply the warranty payment in the “Document

Descriptions of the fields of the screen:

### Field Description

Document Number 11 characters. Required. The document number to

be selected for the warranty payment. This field is
divided in two sections: the prefix and the document
number. If the prefix was set up in the “Document
Number Prefix” field in Configure Warranty
Payments (X11-8), the prefix appears here by
default. Otherwise, you have to position the cursor
to enter it. Once the prefix is entered, it continues to
appear in this field for subsequent entries. The
second part of the document number has to be
entered manually or selected from the Document
Index. The document entered here has to have a
positive unpaid amount. You can not select a credit.

Document # The document numbers already selected for the
payment.

Date The date of the document.

Description The description of the document.

Stock # The stock number of the unit allocated by this
transaction.

Amount The amount of the document.

Dis/Adj. Discount, or the amount of adjustment for this
document.

Screen |: Document Payment

This screen displays all payments already applied to segments on this claim, if
any, and allows you to enter amounts to be applied for the current payment and
associate them with various segments of the claim. Segments are used on this
screen to help you keep track of which parts of the claim have been paid and to
make adjustments accordingly. No distinction is made in the posting batch, where
amounts are combined.

There are ten lines available to enter payments. When the eleventh payment is
applied, the “Claim #” field is changed to “Cumulative” in line 10, the amount of
line 1 is added to the amount of line 10, and line 1 becomes available for entering
anew amount. As additional claim numbers are added, the amount in the #1
position is added to the “Cumulative” line.

After you have entered the amount to credit the warrantor and the amount of the
discount or adjustment (optional—discounts and adjustments can be entered
later), press [Cmd3] to return to the Accounts Receivable Detail screen, where
you can process the next claim.

Automatic Adjustment

There are different ways to enter discount or adjustment amounts on documents.
You can enter amounts for each of the transactions, or you can enter a single
amount for all of the transactions. The [Cmd16] - Automatic Adjustment key can
help you in completing the task. Here is information on the results of using
automatic adjustment and manual adjustment for different situations:

1. The total amount paid is equal to the unpaid amount of the claim (Diff. = 0).
O [Cmdi6]: Without entering the amount, press [Cmd16]. The system
applies the unpaid amount of the claim automatically to the first “Claim #”

line available. You do not have to press [Cmd3] - Return, to leave this
claim.

O Manually: Enter the amounts paid in the “Claim #” fields and press
[Enter]. The payment is applied to the claim. To leave this claim, press
[Cmd3] - Return.

2. The total amount paid is different from the unpaid amount of the claim.

O [Cmd16]: Enter the amounts paid in the “Claim #” fields without entering
the discount/adjustment. Press [Cmd16]. The system calculates the
difference between the unpaid amount of the claim and the total amount
paid, adjusts the total amount paid to the unpaid amount of the claim and
puts the difference in the discount/adjustment field. To leave this claim,
press [Cmd3} - Retum.

Manually: Enter the amounts requested in the “Claim #” fields and enter
the differences in the “Dis/Adj.” fields. To record the information, press
[Enter]. To leave this claim, press [Cmd3] - Return.

3. Transactions are not all paid by this warranty payment.

CO) If the manufacturer pays less than the claim, you have to manually enter
the amounts and discounts/adjustments for the transactions that are paid.
Also, the discount/adjustment can only be entered at the time of the full
payment of the claim. At this point, you will be able to use the [Cmd16] -
Automatic Adjustment key.

Note: During an automatic adjustment with amounts that you have entered (option
2, above), the system verifies the “ Maximum Difference To Adjust
Automatically” that was set up in Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8). If the
difference to be adjusted exceeds this amount, you will receive an error message
telling you than the automatic adjustment can not be made. You can then enter the
adjustment manually. This verification insures that when the adjustment exceeds


16 X11-7 e ENTER WARRANTY PAYMENTS RELEASE 2.1
a eeRELEASE 21

the maximum for automatic adjustment, you are made aware of the adjustment

amount.

C To record the payment of this document, and return to the Accounts
Receivable Detail screen, press [Cmd3] - Return.

Q To have the system automatically apply the payment to documents beginning
with the oldest, press [Cmd16] - Automatic Adjustment.

0) To delete the document, press [Cmd19] - Delete Document.
Descriptions of the fields of the screen:

Field
Claim #

Dis/Adj.

Total Applied

Diff.

Description
Claim numbers are composed of two parts and are

determined by the “Claim Number Different From
Document Number” and “Suffix For Claim
Numbers” fields under Configure Warranty
Payments (X11-8): If the “Claim Number Different
From Document Number” field is set to “N” (No)
claim numbers are the first eight characters of the
selected document number followed by the “Suffix
For Claim Numbers.” If the “Claim Number
Different From Document Number” field is set to
“Y” (Yes), claim numbers are composed of the
claim number entered in the “Claim Number” field
and the “Suffix For Claim Numbers” from
Configure Warranty Payments (X11-8).

Amount to be applied for this claim. The amount
can not be negative.

This field represents the difference between the
claim amount and the amount paid by the
manufacturer. If the payment is higher than the
claim, enter a negative Dis/Adj. amount. If the
payment is lesser, enter a positive Dis/Adj. amount.
The value of this field must be smaller than, or
equal to, the amount entered the “Amount” field.
The “Dis/Adj.” field is an information field only
and does not change the warranty payment.

The total amount paid, the total of discounts/
adjustments as well as the difference between these
two fields for the processed claim.

The difference between the unpaid amount for this
claim and the total amount applied (before
discount/adjustment).

X11-8 « CONFIGURE WARRANTY PAYMENTS

## CHAPTER X11-9

CALCULATE AND POST INTEREST

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to calculate and post interest to your

receivables. During this procedure, interest will be calculated for:

~ all invoices whose age is over the limit set up in the “Days Before Int” field,
under the Security and Configuration Menu (X6-6). The limit set up in the
Security and Configuration Menu is the default for all customer invoices.

— invoices for specific customers over the limit set up in their “Number Of Days
To Charge Interest” field under Receivables Maintenance (X1 1-2)

— specific invoices that are over the limit set up in the “Days Interest” field
under Apply Credits (X11-4)

Interest calculated by the system is displayed onscreen and can be changed before
it is posted. The amount of interest can not be greater than the balance due. If a
customer owes less than the minimum interest charge, you’ll have to change the
amount of interest to be less than or equal to the balance due.

Interest will not be calculated for customers having “N” in the “Charge Interest”

field under Receivables Maintenance (X11-2) or for an invoice with the value
“999” in the “Days Interest” field under Apply Credits (X11-4).

NOTE

The only way to calculate and post interest to all receivables accounts is from the
Calculate and Post Interest option. Make sure it has been run before printing
statements.


2 X11-9 « CALCULATE AND POST INTEREST RELEASE 2.2

### Contents

UNDERSTANDING INTEREST CALCULATIONS ........cssscsscsssssssesseeseesees 3

### Understanding Interest Calculations

The purpose of this section is to explain how interest is calculated and suggest
ways you can make it work effectively for your business.

Transactions are aged in real time, meaning that if you allow a 30-day grace
period, a transaction is current until the 31st day after it is created. Interest is
charged for the whole month on transactions that will be over their allotted
number of days as of the end of the month.

Example I. A transaction (T) charged on May 28 is still current (less than 30
days) on June 25, but it will be over 30 days old on June 30. If you calculate and
post interest (I), then run statements (S) on June 25, interest will be charged on a
current transaction for the entire month of June when it appears on the customer's
statement for the first time.

 

         
   
 

; June 1998
5/28 transaction [Sun_[Mon [Tue [Wed [Thurs [Fri [Sat]
will be current but passe
interest will be A EE

applied for the p14 fis tie a7 4a 49 [20

 
 

month of June

|21__ [227 [a3 [ea [asus [26 [a7 |
[28 [29 30

        

If you don't want this to happen, but you want to continue running statements on
the 25th, you can change “Days Before Int” field in Security Maintenance (X6-6)
to a number higher than 30. The number will be based on the day you actually run
statements: 30 (Number of days in month)-25 (Day you charge interest)=6
(Difference); 30 (Current setting) + 5 (Difference) = 35 (New setting).

In the example above, with 35 days before interest is charged, the 5/28 transaction
will be current until July 1, and no interest will be charged on June 25.


4 X11-9 e CALCULATE AND POST INTEREST RELEASE 2.2

This setting can be changed as often as you like so it can accommodate February {
and months with 31 days. Don't forget that "Number of Days to Charge Interest"

can be changed on the customer's master record (Receivables Maintenance X11-2)

and at the invoice level in Apply Credits (X11-4).

Example 2. A transaction (T) charged on May 1 is still current (less than 30 days)
on May 25, and it will still be current on May 31. If you calculate and post interest
(J), then run statements (S) on May 25, no interest will be charged.

The 5/1 transaction falls into the 30-day category on June 4. If the transaction is
paid (P) on June 24, the customer will not be charged any interest when it is
calculated on June 25. In this case, the customer has enjoyed 20 additional
interest-free days. However, if the transaction has not been paid when interest is
calculated on June 25, interest will be charged for the entire month of June.

A strategy adopted by some dealers is to establish a due date, such as the 10th of
the month. It is clearly indicated on the customer's statement that they must pay by
the 10th to avoid interest charges. On the 11th, interest (I) is calculated and posted
even though statements (S) are not printed until the 25th.

### - Calculate And Post Interest 5

In this case, the 5/1 transaction that is paid (P) on the 24th is still charged interest
(X) for the month of June on the statement (S) that is printed on the 25th.

Remember to calculate and post interest only once a month! On the selection
screen, which is illustrated below, make sure you are calculating interest for the
current month only. In the example, note that interest was last calculated on
3/25/98. It is now 6/25/98. If you indicate that you want to calculate interest for a
future month by entering 0798, interest will be calculated for 2 full months on
every transaction. If you make a mistake, (you'll notice that the interest is too
high), press Cmd1-End from the Update Interest screen. Do not post the batch
unless you enjoy making corrections!

Notes:

## CHAPTER X11-10

PRINT STATEMENTS

### Introduction

‘You can print statements at any time, more than once a month, if desired. When
you print statements, current transactions for balance forward customers are
moved to the balance forward total for the next billing. If you don’t want to
change current transactions so that they will be printed on the next statement, run
Interim/Past Due Statements (X11-11) instead. To calculate and Post interest, ran
Calculate And Post Interest (X11-9).

Customers can be selected by general ledger account (all receivables, or up to ten
individual accounts), group code, or address number (all, or up to ten individual
customers).

‘You can choose to print non-posted interest on the statements (optional). If you
choose to print unposted interest, it is included in the total balance due on
statements. If a customer pays the unposted interest from their statement, post the
unapplied credit, then make a journal entry to post the interest. Use Apply Credits
to merge the payment with the interest. If you rn Calculate & Post Interest (X11-
9) and then say “Yes to print unposted interest for the same general ledger period,
you will have double interest on that month's statement. Printing unposted interest
is a way to handle customers who don't pay interest but you wish they would. Deal
with it if they pay instead of having to back it out if they don't.

Print Statements will display all transactions since the last time Print Statements
was run for both balance forward and open item statements. For balance forward
Statements, payments listed on the previous statement will be applied to previous
invoices and the unpaid balance will appear as the balance forward total. For open
item statements, payments listed on the previous statement will be applied to
previous invoices and unpaid transactions will be listed as open items.

If you want to reprint a statement exactly like the one a customer received, contact
your DIS Marketing Representative about Archiving.

ACCOUNTING X11-10 « PRINT STATEMENTS 5
eS OE MENS

The prompt, “Calculate non-posted interest,” refers to whether you want to
calculate and print interest that has not been posted. It can be used to calculate
interest for the next month: the G/L Period (MMYY) refers to the month you want
to calculate interest for. Remember interest is always calculated for an entire
month. You’ ll want to coordinate the number of days before interest is charged,
the date you actually post interest, and the date for printing statements with non-
posted interest.

For example, you might decide to age accounts and post interest on the 20th of
each month and delay printing statements until the 25th. To let customers know
that you expect payment by the 20th and that they will be charged interest if they
delay payment, you can have next month’s interest calculated and printed on their
statements. You won’t actually post the interest until the 20th of the next month;
however, the interest will be added to the total balance due as if it had been
posted. If a customer pays the interest before it has been posted, you can either
credit their account or make a journal entry to post the interest charge.

    
  

### Warning

   

If you choose to print unposted interest, it is included in the total balance due on
statements. If a customer pays the unposted interest from their statement, post the
unapplied credit, then make a journal entry to post the interest. Use Apply Credits
to merge the payment with the interest. If you run Calculate & Post Interest (X11-
9) and then say "Yes" to print unposted interest for the same general ledger
period, you will have double interest on that month's statement. Printing unposted
interest is a way to handle customers who don't, pay interest but you wish they
would. Deal with it if they pay instead of having to back it out if they don't.

 
       
 
         

O To calculate interest to print on statements, type ¥ in the “Calculate non-
posted interest” field. This interest will not be posted to your customer
accounts. The only way to post interest in Receivables is from the option
Calculate And Post Interest (X11-9).

0 If you choose to calculate interest here, in the “Interest Transactions (non-
posted)” field, enter the document number, the description for interest
transactions, and the general ledger month for the calculation of interest.
INTEREST is the default document number. The description is optional. In
the “G/L Period” field, enter-the general ledger month for calculating the
interest in the format MMYY (month, year). You can print for any period. To
print statements for the current month, leave this field blank.

### How To Print And Align Statements

When you press [Cmd2] - Continue, from the Update Interest screen (if you have
chosen to calculate non-posted interest), or you press [Cmd2] - Continue, from the
Update Receivables Messages screen (if you have chosen not to calculate
interest), the statements are generated and sent to the print queue.

NOTE

Options allowing you to print your statements in various ways can be set up in the

OPTDIS Master Menu (X6-3) under the “Receivables” option. Review the
documentation on the OPTDIS Master Menu or see the Accounts Receivable
Guide to New Features for complete information.

 

Forms alignment is not an exact science: printers of the same make and model
may be calibrated differently. Your own printer won't maintain the same
alignment forever. As any mechanic can tell you, anything with moving parts
changes!

Even on the same printer, it helps to think about forms alignment as a process, not
something that you do right the first time every time. The most important part of
the process is to become comfortable with the system messages and how to
answer them.

In general the process goes like this:
O Load the forms.

O Print the first line. Make adjustment.


14 X11-10 ¢ PRINT STATEMENTS RELEASE 2.2
Fy eS 22

C) Print the first line again. Make adjustment. Repeat this step until you are pretty (
sure you have the alignment OK. On the AS/400, you do not have the option
to print one line at a time. Your choices are to print the same line on the same
form, print the same line on the next form, or print the next line and continue
without further messages. You don’t ever want to cancel the print job. Of
course, with pre-printed checks you don’t even want to skip to the next form,
so your choices are even more limited.

C Let them print! If you need to make another minor adjustment, take the
printer off-line temporarily. It will resume exactly where it left off when you
put it back on-line. If you have a forms jam or other semi-catastrophe, see the
section "What Can Go Wrong & What To Do” in the Appendix chapter that
applies to your printer.

Q Remove the special forms and reload standard paper.

Each step is controlled through system messages and your answers to them.
Following the instructions about physical alignment will help you get started;
however, you'll need to figure out what works best on your printer and mark the
diagrams accordingly.

### System Messages (

The DIS Business System recognizes 4 different forms for the system printer:

Form System Abbreviation
1. Standard STD or 0001

2. Checks CHKS

3. Statements STAT

4. Labels LAB

5. Letters LETT

The stock paper used for reports is called "Standard," whether it is wide bar or 8
1/2" X 11" letter-size. To prevent your accidentally printing important things like
checks on standard paper, or reports on expensive forms such as checks, the
system always lets you know when it is time to change forms.

System messages tell you when to load special forms, such as statements, and
when to reload regular standard paper; however, it must depend on your answers
to the messages to “know” what kind of forms are currently in the printer. In
addition, when your answer indicates that forms have been changed, the system


ACCOUNTING X11-10 « PRINT STATEMENTS 15
ET AT EMENTO UN

provides a message to facilitate alignment. In its own clunky mechanical way, it is
trying to make your job easier.

Although there seem to be dozens of messages the first time you try to align -
forms, there are really only 2 different messages: .
- Load Forms, which comes at the beginning and end of a job that requires
different forms.
«Alignment, which can be repeated as often as necessary.

Your success depends on having the forms almost right when you answer the
Load Forms message and then controlling adjustments through the Alignment
message.

When you run a job that requires a change of forms, look at the AS/400's “Work
with Printer Output” screen. At any DIS menu, type: D P [Enter]. The screen is
illustrated below. In the example, messages for Past Due Statements (XI 1-9) is
illustrated.

Screen i: Additional Message information

O1 To see more information, press [Page Down].

The Load Forms message, CPA3394, is the first message and it occurs once at the
beginning and once at the end.of the job. It is displayed when it is time to take the
stock paper out of the printer and put statements in or vice versa. The possible
answers to this message are:
H= Hold
C =Cancel
G= Go. Answer with a '"G" after the specified forms (statements) are loaded.
This is the answer you'll use most of the time. It signals the computer
that forms have been changed to checks (CHKS) or statements (STAT).
I= Ignore the request for changing forms and use the forms currently on the
printer.

R=Retry

The Load Forms message is issued again at the end of the job as soon as the
system is ready to print a report or anything that uses forms other than checks or : CL


X11-10 « PRINT STATEMENTS 7

statements. The procedure is the same: Answer with a "
forms are loaded.

 

" after the specified

A COMMON MISTAKE is to take out the statements and reload-standard paper ~
before this message is received. The same problem arises when standard forms are
removed and special forms loaded before the Load Forms message.

it then seems logical to answer the Load Forms message with an "I," which means
you don't want to change forms and that you want to continue on the current
forms. The trouble is that now you think "current forms" are standard but the
system still thinks "current forms" are checks or statements.

If you find yourself in this situation, to change the forms number and restart the
print job, follow the instructions in the section “What Can Go Wrong & What To
Do” in the Appendix chapter that applies to your printer.

THE BEST PROCEDURE is:
O Don't do anything until you receive the Load Forms message.

(1 When you receive the message, don't answer it immediately. :
O Change the forms as instructed. .
QO Answer with a G to indicate that you have done what the system requested. -

The Alignment message, CPA4002, is displayed immediately after the first line is
printed. The possible answers to this message are:

I =To continue printing aligned forms starting with the next line of the file,
type an I. Statements are printed without further messages.

C =To cancel processing, type aC. DO NOT USE THIS OPTION. You
cannot re-run Monthly Billing or Print Payables Checks or Payroll unless
you delete your data files and restore a backup, which means you may
have to repeat a lot of work.

G= To continue printing aligned forms skipping to the next form and
printing the first line again, type a G. The first check or statement is
printed on the next form and no additional Alignment messages are
presented.

N= To print the first line again on the next form and to verify the alignment,
O Press [Stop] only if [Start] and [Stop] are two keys, or press [Reset].
Advance the paper to the next form by pressing [Form Feed/New

Page].
O Adjust the alignment with the forms adjust control.
O Press [Ready], [Start], or [Start/Stop].
D Type ann.

R =To print the first line again on the current form and to verify the alignment
if the forms are not aligned,

O Press [Stop] only if [Start] and [Stop] are two keys, or press [Reset].
O Adjust the alignment with the forms adjust control.

O Press [Ready], [Start], or [Start/Stop}.

O Type an rR.

After you have "authorized" the printing job to proceed without further
interruption, you can still make adjustments by taking the printer off-line
temporarily. Do not turn the printer off! Pressing “Start/Stop” simply suspends
printing and the job resumes at exactly the same place in the file when the printer
is placed back on-line. This allows you to roll the paper in tiny increments fine
tuning alignment as the statements are being printed.

‘You may want to save output before printing, in case you are having problems
with alignment or would simply like additional copies. The following is an
example of saving output from statements.

## CHAPTER X11-11

PRINT INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to allow you to print interim or past due statements for
selected receivables. You can print Interim/Past Due Statements at any time.
Current transactions (activity since the most recent regular statement) will be
listed. Customers can be selected based on the Number of Days That Make
Collection Critical, which is set up by customer in Receivables Maintenance
(X11-2). The Aged Receivables Collection Report, which shows trending
information, is also based on the same field.

Print Interim/Past Due Statements will display all transactions since the last time
Print Statements (X11-10) was run for both balance forward and open item
Statement types. Print Interim/Past Due Statements can be run repeatedly without
affecting the status of transactions in accounts. Current transactions will not be
merged into balance forward and will appear as current transactions the next time
Print Statements is run.

To calculate and post interest, run Calculate And Post Interest (X11-9). To print
Statements in your regular cycle, run Print Statements (X11-10).

If you want to reprint a statement exactly like the one a customer received, contact
your DIS Marketing Representative about Archiving.


2 X11-11 ¢ PRINT INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS RELEASE 2.2

### Entrance Screen

O From the Receivables Menu (X1-1), select option 11, Print Interim/Past Due
Statements and press [Enter]. The Print Interim Statements, Selection screen
appears:

NW EQUIPMENT SALES PRINT INTERIM STATEMENTS X11B01-01
Division A Selection

2-Zip Code, Name
3-Address Number

: 1-General Ledger Account
2-Group Code

3-Address Number

Screen A: Print interim Statements, Selection

Statements can be run for 1-10 selected customers, all customers, or 1-10 groups
based on group code. In addition, customers can be selected by the age of their
accounts, such as current, 30, 60, 90, and 120+ and Messages can be entered for
each age category as in previous releases.

### Parameter Selection

C1 In the “Include Paid Invoices and Payments” field, to include paid invoices
and payments type Y, or to include only current, unpaid invoices, type N.

O Enter one of the following parameters to determine how customer accounts
will be sorted for statement printing:
1 =Sort by the customer name
2 = Sort by the zip code and the customer name
3 = Sort by the customer address number


X11-11 « PRINT INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS RELEASE 2.2

1 Enter one of the following parameters to determine how customers will be
selected for statements:

1 = Select by general ledger account or all customers
2 = Select by group code
3 = Select by address number

O] Press [Enter] to continue.

O Press [Cmd1] - End, to exit the procedure without printing interim or past due
statements.

Select By General Ledger Account

by G/L Accounts screen appears:

specific general ledger accounts, the selected accounts must be included in the
division displayed in the upper left corner of the screen. Accounts must also
be valid and active in the general ledger chart of accounts and they have to
have an edit code of “A” (accounts receivable).

return to the Receivables Menu (X1-1), press [Cmd1] - End.

### How To Print And Align Statements

From the Update Receivables Messages screen, when you ‘press [Cmd2] -
Continue, the statements are generated and sent to the job queue.

O To return to the Accounts Receivable Menu, press [Enter].

NOTE

Options allowing you to print your statements in various ways can be set up in the
OPTDIS Master Menu (X6-3) under the “Receivables” option. Review the
documentation on the OPTDIS Master Menu for complete information.

 

Interim/Past Due statements are printed on the system printer on statement forms
(STAT). Watch the print spool by typing: D P [Enter] at a command line. You'll
see the job on the print spool with a message waiting. Select it with 7=Message.

For further instructions, see “How to Print and Align Statements” in Print
Statements (X11-10).

Examples of statements in balance forward and open item modes follow.

INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS

Open Item Statement

If there has been no activity on an open item statement, it will be identical to the
most recent regular statement unless aging has caused amounts to shift to the next
aging category, such as 30 days to 60 days.

Balance Forward Statement

Transactions that were listed as current on the most recent balance forward
statement in Print Statements will be included in the balance forward on an
interim statement. Current transactions (activity since the most recent regular


10 X11-17 ¢ PRINT INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS RELEASE 2.2
SS EE

statement) are not affected (rolled into balance forward), when interim statements
are run, so they will be listed on the next regular statement.

Corporate Statement

The following corporate statement is 3 pages long and incorporates statements
from the following receivables: Austin Construction, Inc. (A00960), which is the
corporate account, plus its subsidiaries: BO4070, C06700, and G12512.

X11-11 « PRINT INTERIM/PAST DUE STATEMENTS

## CHAPTER X11-12

LETTERS MAINTENANCE

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to write and save letters, which will be sent to charge
customers. Only address numbers in the receivables file are used for letters. A list
of outstanding invoices in any aging category may be attached as an appendix to
any letter. Although variables, such as names and addresses, even balances, may

be embedded in letters, the actual recipients are selected in option 13, Print
Letters.

### Contents

   
  
 
 
 

ENTRANCE SCREEN
CREATING A NEW LETTER...
LETTER DETAIL

Using Variables...
Inserting or Moving Lines
CHANGING A LETTER.

DELETING A LETTER..

6 X11-12 ¢ LETTERS MAINTENANCE RELEASE 2.1

Symbolic Variables
Letters can be personalized by embedding codes that will be teplaced by the
current system date, information from customers’ master records, balances, etc.

O To see the list of variables, press [Help] ([Alt}{F1] on some keyboards) from
the detail screen.

 

Symbolic variables

 
  
  
  
 
   
 

The symbolic variables allow you to merge your customer fields in your
letters. You must reserve the appropriate number of characters needed for
the printing of these fields. Each available variable is listed with its
corresponding length, the "@xx" is part of the length to reserve,

Variable Description-------- * Lgth Variable Description-------- * Lgth
201 Name 28 @12 90 Days 13
02 Name (Ext) 15 @13° 120 Days 13
@03° Address 20 @14  - Interest/Balance 13
@04 0 Address (Ext) 20 @1S Credit Limit 6
eos = City, State 20 @16 Our Vendor Number to
@06 = Zip Code 9 @17 AP. Clerk (Name) 28
@07 0 Address # 6 @18 Session Date MM/DD/YY 8
@08 = Total Balance 23 @19 Session Date DD/MM/YY 8
e@09 Current 13 @20 Session Date YY¥/MM/DD 8
@10 30 Days 13 @21 Session Date (*) 1s
@11 60 Days 13

Enter-End Help (*) = Date With Month In Letters (ex.: September 15, 1995)

 

Screen E: Symbolic Variables

co


X11-12 e LETTERS MAINTENANCE 7

Using Variables

In the column labeled “Lgth,” you'll find the number of spaces you need to allow
for the variable, such as Name, which has a length of 28 characters. The 3
character variable, such as @01, is included in the length you need to reserve. For
example, reserve exactly 8 spaces for a date, not 8+ 3 =11.

Names

To print the customer's name after “Dear” leave | space after “Dear” and then
type the code, which is @01. The line will look like this:
Dear @01

There must be 25 blank spaces after the @01. Because not every name will take
the allotted 28 characters, don't include a colon (:) at the end or you'll end up with
something that looks like this:

Dear Gerry Parker

Dollar Amounts

If you want to include balances, you may want to include dollar signs.

Here is a line that will include a balance:
Your current balance, which is $@09 , Must be
paid before we can extend credit privileges again.

The result:
Your current balance, which is $57.33 , Must be
paid before we can extend credit privileges again.

Again, there is a problem with punctuation following the variable.

Dates

Dates are easier, because their length is dependable.
Pay within 30 days of today, @18

The result:
Pay within 30 days of today, 8/07/97.
Avoiding Punctuation

Wherever you have a variable that may not be as long as the space allowed, try to
arrange your sentences so that it is at the end and omit the punctuation.

12 X11-12 « LETTERS MAINTENANCE RELEASE 2.1

Notes:

## CHAPTER X11-13

PRINT LETTERS

### Introduction

The purpose of this job is to select the target audience and print letters that were
created in Letters Maintenance (X1 1-12). Letters can be sorted by Name,
Address#, or Zip Code and addressed to customers selected by: G/L Account;
Group Code; Address Number; Age Category; Area, Zip, Sort, or Edit Codes. An
optional appendix may be attached listing outstanding transactions.

Only receivables addresses are eligible to receive letters. They have an edit code
of “R” in position 4, which is assigned when they are brought up in Receivables
Maintenance (X11-2). Mailing labels can also be printed (optional). The first
mailing label is for alignment. Letters and labels are printed on the system printer
on letter forms (LETT) and label forms (LAB).

### Contents

6 X11-13 e PRINT LETTERS RELEASE 2.1

 

4-Age Category

NW EQUIPMENT SALES PRINT LETTERS X11D01-06
Division A Selection By Age Category

Enter The Age Category For The Customers To Print ...

*000' = All Customers With Balances

‘030' = Customers With 30 Days Past Due Balances
*060' = Customers With 60 Days Past Due Balances
*090' Customers With 90 Days Past Due Balances
‘120' = Customers With 120 Days Past Due Balances

Notice! The letter you selected will be printed for all customers
in the age category you select and all customers in all higher
age categories. Example: Selecting 060 will result in letters to

### Examples

Letters are designed for standard 8.5"x11" paper. Labels are designed for
4"x15/16" high labels, 1 across. See the Appendix of the DIS User Manual for
information related to printer messages and how to answer them. A sample letter
with a transaction appendix follows.

Sample Letter

October 1, 1996

PALMO1
RUTH PALMER

P.O. BOX i14
DYSART, IOWA T7777 7442

Dear RUTH PALMER
According to our records, your total balance is: $ 458.55
Of this, the following amount is over 120 days past due: ¢ 458.55.

This is really unacceptable and we insist on immediate payment;
otherwise, we have no choice but to turn this account over to our
attorney, Doberman Dan. This will not be a pleasant experience for
you. Save yourself and your family from the humiliation of having
Mr. Dan hang you out to dry in court.

So let's please get with the program, RUTH PALMER
Send us your check in the amount of $ 458.55 .

We are, as always, waiting for your payment--hope to see it soon...

Ura Hogg
NW Equipment Sales

2/15/97 FEB ROA

3/15/97 INT CHG
3/15/97 Iv00024 #* INVOICE
3/15/57 ROA MAR
4/30/97 INT CHG

10/15/97 INT CHE

above. Also, characters from the Receivables Maintenance screen are all caps, a
legacy of the S/36 environment.
